style=\"letter-spacing: -0.2pt;\"> </span>q<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.25pt;\">u</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.15pt;\">a</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.25pt;\">n</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.15pt;\">t</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">it</span>y<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.2pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.1pt;\">s</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.25pt;\">h</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.25pt;\">o</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.3pt;\">w</span>n<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.4pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.25pt;\">o</span>n<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.15pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.15pt;\">t</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.25pt;\">h</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.1pt;\">O</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.25pt;\">u</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">tt</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.25pt;\">u</span>rn<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.2pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.05pt;\">C</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.4pt;\">e</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.25pt;\">r</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.15pt;\">t</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">i</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.25pt;\">f</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">i</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.15pt;\">c</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">at</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.15pt;\">e</span>.</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-right: -1.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Procedure</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">: Load on top is the shipboard procedure of collecting and settling water and oil mixtures, resulting from ballasting and tank cleaning operations (usually in a special slop tank or tanks), and subsequently loading cargo on top of and pumping the mixture ashore at the discharge port. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Practice</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">: Load on top is the act of commingling on-board quantity with cargo being loaded. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Loaded Passage</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The passage during which the tanker is carrying cargo. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Long Ton</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A unit of weight = 2,240 pounds or 1,106 kilos. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Marine Custody Transfer (MCT)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A custody transfer activity involving a marine tank vessel(s). Loading, discharging or lightering a ship or barge is a marine custody transfer.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Marine Surveyor</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A duly qualified person who examines ships to ascertain their condition, on behalf of owners, underwriters, etc. Also called \"ship surveyor\" or simply \"surveyor\". <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Maritime Law</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - That system of jurisprudence that prevails in courts having jurisdiction of marine causes. Also called marine or admiralty law. It is a branch of both international and commercial law. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Metric Ton</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> \u2013 A unit of weight 2,204.6 pounds (1,000 kilograms). <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Midship Draft</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The draft read at the midship markings. This draft can, and often does, differ from the Mean Draft due to hogging or sagging. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Net Registered Tonnage</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The internal capacity of a vessel measured in units of 100 cubic feet less the space occupied by boilers, engines, shaft alleys, chain lockers, officer\u2019s and crew quarters and other spaces not available for carrying passengers or freight. Net registered tonnage is usually referred to as registered tonnage or net tonnage. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Net Tonnage</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The volumetric cargo capacity of a ship expressed on the basis of 100 cubic feet to the ton. On passenger vessels it also includes space used by passengers. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">OBQ (On Board Quantity)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The material remaining in vessel tanks, void spaces, and/or pipelines prior to loading. On-board quantity includes water, oil, slops, oil residue, oil/water emulsions, sludge, and sediment. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">OCIMF </span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">\u2013 The oil companies\u2019 international marine forum is an organization of oil companies that own or operate ships.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Outage (Ullage)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The depth of the space in a tank not occupied by oil. Same as ullage. It is measured from the flange of the ullage hole to the surface of the oil. Also the space left in a petroleum product container to allow for expansion as a result of temperature changes during shipment and use. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Out-Turn Certificate</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A document issued by the receivers of cargo indicating the amount of cargo&nbsp;</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><a href=\"http://www.blogger.com/post-edit.g?blogID=3564735312144269387&amp;postID=4065337653729326015\" name=\"P\"><b><i><span style=\"color: maroon;\"><br />\n</span></i></b></a></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Panamax</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The maximum size ship that can fit through the Panama Canal in terms of width, length and draft generally about 80,000dwt. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Plimsoll Mark</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The mark on the side of a classed vessel which indicates its safe load lines at varying seasonal conditions. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Port Charges</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - General term which includes charges and dues of every nature assessed against the vessel or its cargo in a port. It usually includes harbor dues, tub boat charges, pilotage fees, custom house fees, consular fees, etc. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Port State</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> \u2013 A state that has ports to which ships call. The port state makes regulations the calling ships must adhere to. The port state control is the controlling authority of the port state on shipping such as the coast guard or naval authorities</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Port Time (Two Types)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> \u2013 1) Seabuoy to Seabuoy - The time elapsed between the vessel\u2019s passing the port\u2019s seabuoy upon entrance to re-passing it upon exit. It includes time for steaming in and out of berth, delays, hose connections, anchorage time, clearing and loading or unloading time. 2) Port to Port - Includes only time for delays, hose connections, anchorage time, clearing and loading or unloading time. Use must be consistent with voyage mileage basis. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Portable Measurement Unit (PMU)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A device designed to measure the ship\u2019s cargo when its tanks are closed to the atmosphere. It is used in conjunction with a vapor control valve. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Portable Sampling Unit (PSU)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A device designed to sample the ship\u2019s cargo when its tanks are closed to the atmosphere. It is used in conjunction with a vapor control valve. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Pressure/Vacuum Valve (P/V Valve)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - An automatic dual purpose valve, commonly fitted in the vent lines of tankers. When in the closed position, the function of this valve is to relieve either pressure or vacuum in a tank. When in the open position it allows the passage of air or vapor into and out of the tank. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Reducer</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">- A short section of pipe, having one end of smaller diameter than the other and having a flange on each end, for connecting a smaller hose or pipe to a pipe of constant diameter. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Restricted Measurement System</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> \u2013 A measurement system designed to measure the ship\u2019s cargo when its tanks are closed to the atmosphere. During measurements a minimum amount of cargo vapors might escape to the atmosphere<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 98%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 38.85pt; margin-top: .4pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt; line-height: 98%;\">ROB (Remain on Board)&nbsp;</span></b></span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 13px; line-height: 12px;\">- The material remaining in vessel tanks, void spaces, and/or pipelines after discharge. Remaining on board quantity includes water, oil, slops, oil residue, oil/water emulsions, sludge, and sediment.</span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></b></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Rogue Wave</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> \u2013 An ocean wave much larger than the current wave sequence. This wave may also be outside the current wave direction and may be 100 feet or more in height<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Routing</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A complex of measures concerning routes aimed at reducing the risk of casualties; it includes traffic separation schemes, two-way routes, tracks, areas to be avoided, inshore traffic zones, and deep water routes. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Sag (Sagging)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The condition of a vessel caused by the unequal distribution of cargo. When a vessel loads too heavily in the center it causes a bending downward of the hull at the midships area. This can also be caused by the vessel working in heavy seas with large waves under each end and no support under the center of the ship. Sag is the opposite of Hog. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Sea Trials</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A series of trials conducted by the builders during which the owner\u2019s representatives on board act in a consulting and checking capacity to determine if the vessel has met the specifications. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Seaworthiness</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The sufficiency of a vessel in materials constructions, equipment, crew and outfit for the trade in which the it is employed. Any sort of disrepair to the vessel by which the cargo may suffer; overloading; untrained officers; may constitute a vessel unseaworthy. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Seaworthiness Certificate</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A certificate issued by a classification society surveyor to allow a vessel proceed after she has me with a mishap that may have affected its seaworthiness. It is frequently issued to enable a vessel to proceed, after temporary repairs have been effected, to another port where permanent repairs are then carried out. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Short-Handed</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - Said of a vessel inadequately manned or without the regular number of men. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Sister Ships</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - Ships built on the same design. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Slops</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A mixture of petroleum and water normally arising from tank washings. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Sludge</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A mixture of petroleum and water, usually semi-solid, frequently containing sand and scale. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Special Survey</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The survey requirement of a classification society that usually takes place every four years. At the special survey vital pieces of equipment are opened up and inspected by the classification surveyor. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Stem</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">&nbsp; To order or arrange for, e.g bunkers.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Submarine Loading Terminal</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A terminal where loading is carried out by means of an offshore hose run along the sea bottom. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Suezmax</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> \u2013 The maximize size ship that can sail through the Suez canal generally considered to be between 150-200,000 DWT depending on ships dimensions and draft.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Tender (TO)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A master tenders his vessel when he advises the charterer or supplier that he is ready to load. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Time-Charter</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A form of charter party wherein owner lets or leases his vessel and crew to the charterer for a stipulated period of time. The charterer pays for the bunkers and charges in addition to the hire. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Tonnage Tax</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> \u2013 Taxes, fees, harbor dues etc. paid on the vessel based on a tonnage calculation.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Topping-Off</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - 1) the operation of completing the loading of a tank to a required ullage. 2) Filling up cargo tanks which were only partially filled at the loading port because of port or canal draft restrictions. The filling up occurs outside the loading port via lightering activities, or at another loading port. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; tab-stops: 138.0pt; text-align: justify; text-autospace: none;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"color: black; font-size: 10pt; letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">Total port time</span></b><span style=\"color: black; font-size: 10pt; letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">: T</span><span style=\"color: black; 0.05pt;\">r</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.25pt;\"> </span>H<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">a</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.1pt;\">r</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">b</span>our<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.3pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">S</span>te<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">a</span>mi<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">n</span>g<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.45pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">s</span>ta<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">r</span>ts<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.2pt;\"> </span>a<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">n</span>d <span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">f</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.05pt;\">i</span>n<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">i</span>s<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">h</span>es<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.3pt;\"> </span>for<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.05pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">T</span>a<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">n</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.05pt;\">k</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">e</span>r<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.25pt;\"> </span>Po<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">r</span>t<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.2pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">P</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">r</span>f<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">o</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.1pt;\">r</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">m</span>an<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">c</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.6pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">p</span>u<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">r</span>po<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">s</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">s</span>.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-align: justify; text-autospace: none;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Track</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The recommended direction or path to be followed when proceeding between pre-determined position. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Traffic</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - Movement of shipping. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Traffic Lane</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - An area within definite limits inside which one-way traffic is established. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Traffic Separation Scheme</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A scheme which separates traffic proceeding in opposite or nearly opposite directions by the use of a separation zone or line, traffic lanes or by other means. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Underwriter</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">- In marine insurance one who subscribes his name to the policy indicating his acceptance of the liability mentioned therein consideration for which he receives a premium. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Unseaworthiness</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The states or condition of a vessel when it is not in a proper state of maintenance, or if the loading equipment or crew, or in any other respect is not ready to encounter the ordinary perils of sea. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Used Laytime</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The amount of lay time that was taken by the vessel for loading and discharging on a voyage. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Vapor Control Valve (VCV)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> \u2013 This valves is used in conjunction with closed and restricted measurement equipment to allow measurements in ship\u2019s tanks that are closed to the atmosphere. Once a portable measurement unit (PMU) is attached to the VCV, the valve is opened and the PMU\u2019s probe is dropped into the tank to perform the required measurements.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Vapor Recovery System (VRS)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - Procedures and equipment for the collection of hydrocarbon vapors from vessel\u2019s tanks and the transfer to shoreside recovery equipment. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Vessel Experience Factor (VEF)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A factor based on the compilation of the history of the total calculated volume (TCV) vessel measurements, adjusted for on-board quantity (OBQ) or remaining on board (ROB), compared with the TCV shore measurements. This factor if developed according to the latest industry standards may be used to obtain a better ship shore comparison of volumes.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Vetting</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The general process of approving a vessel for use.&nbsp; (From old English \"To Vet\" - to look at or review again.)&nbsp; Note: actual procedure varies from company to company. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Wall Wash Test</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The procedure of introducing an appropriate liquid into a vessel\u2019s tank to test for hydrocarbon, color and other contaminants. This test is done by physically pouring the liquid down vessel\u2019s tank bulkheads and trapping a portion on filter paper. This test is also done on vessel\u2019s steam coils and sumps.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Watertight Door</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A door so constructed that, when closed, it will prevent water under pressure from passing through.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Water/Cut Measurement</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - The procedure of locating the oil/water interface for the purpose of determining the volume of free water in a shore tank or vessel compartment. It is also used to refer to the line of demarcation of the oil/water interface.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Wedge Formula</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A mathematical means to approximate small quantities of liquid and solid cargo and free water on board prior to loading and after discharge based on cargo compartment dimensions and vessel trim. The wedge formula is to be used only when the liquid does not touch all bulk heads of the vessel\u2019s tanks.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\">Wedge Table</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"> - A pre-calculated vessel table based on the wedge formula and displayed much like the vessel\u2019s usual innage/ullage tables. These tables, however, are for small quantities (on- board quantities, remaining on board) when the cargo or free water does not touch all bulkheads of the vessel tank.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Wipe Test</span></span></b><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"> - The procedure of physically wiping random interior areas and steam coils of vessel\u2019s tanks with absorbent white rags. This procedure is used to test the tank\u2019s coating for possible color contamination.</span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-DfEyhIqSJ1E/TVY7QhzQ2GI/AAAAAAAADZ8/AoGE4lZpjo4/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-DfEyhIqSJ1E/TVY7QhzQ2GI/AAAAAAAADZ8/AoGE4lZpjo4/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">-------CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL ( 28 YEARS IN COMMAND )<o:p></o:p></span></div></div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "2", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/4065337653729326015/comments"}}, {"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "1963295117232337821", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2011-02-12T07:32:00+05:30", "updated": "2013-08-16T19:26:52+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxMzc2NjYxNDEyNzI0Cm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2011/02/are-you-mentally-sick-capt-ajit.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/1963295117232337821", "title": "ARE YOU MENTALLY SICK --  CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: left;\" trbidi=\"on\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-tL9J8q1ya80/TVXpc151wkI/AAAAAAAADZA/mqtLJbTSeGE/s1600/images+%25282%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-tL9J8q1ya80/TVXpc151wkI/AAAAAAAADZA/mqtLJbTSeGE/s1600/images+%25282%2529.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\nHOARDING, THE OCD<br />\n<br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red; font-size: large;\"><b>Read this piece and judge for yourself , if you are mentally sick.&nbsp;</b></span><br />\n<br />\nAfter that think about your immediate family and friends. 30% chances are that you have this mental disease called OBSESSIVE COMPULSIVE DISORDER.<br />\n<br />\nAre you a hoarder?<br />\n<br />\nThink of all the cloth in your house--inside wardrobes. attics etc. How many of them will you use for the next 3 years. What is the percentage which you have hoarded?<br />\n<br />\n<br />\n<div style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 0in;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; line-height: 24px;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">Hoarding is an effort to manage the anxiety raised by obsessive doubts.</span> &nbsp;</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; line-height: 24px;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; line-height: 24px;\">There will be &nbsp;a disruption to feelings of self-worth, interpersonal relationships, occupation, or health as a result of hoarding items which are worthless.</span></div>\n<div style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 0in;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; line-height: 24px;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 0in;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; line-height: 24px;\"></span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; line-height: 24px;\">Hoarders experience intense anxiety when they even think of discarding what most others view as useless objects.</span></div>\n<div style=\"margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 0in; margin-top: 0in;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; line-height: 24px;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">They are affected by anxiety-provoking thoughts such as: \"What if I run out?\" \"What if I need to know something and don't have the information available?\" \" \"What if I throw it away but the day comes when I really need it?\"<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-lixWHs3akU0/TVXpgZjI01I/AAAAAAAADZE/cNL3LcxgwKA/s1600/images+%252811%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-lixWHs3akU0/TVXpgZjI01I/AAAAAAAADZE/cNL3LcxgwKA/s1600/images+%252811%2529.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Hoarding usually starts in an attic, then in a basement, a spare room, a closet, and then, eventually, takes over every room of the house. As their mounds of useless items continue to climb toward the ceiling, their home is no longer a home. &nbsp;Room after room ceases to function. What was once a normal, functional home becomes room after room of trash bins. You look under the bed you will find dust and trash.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Strong emotional connections are formed to the extent that an individual feels a sense of safety or comfort.&nbsp; Hoarders are suspicious of other people touching possessions , as they feel it may be thrown away , when they are not around.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">If you are not a hoarder, but your friend is, it is your duty to help him to change. Convince him that being overly sentimental does not bring happiness---that storing up stuff only brings misery, chaos, and isolation. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Get him involved in dividing his stuff into 4 groups. \u201cKeepers\u201d, \u201cDonations\u201d, \u201cTo Sell\u201d, and \u201cGarbage.\u201d There is no point in throwing stuff away when your hoarder friend or relative is out of town. Be sure the hoarder stands at the front door and grants the final \u201cOK\u201d on each item. It\u2019s vital that he makes the earth shakin\u2019 decision of what to do with his garbage stuff. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-bI2Pj4YEzV0/TVXpjJTVM5I/AAAAAAAADZI/1Je6dlxs3To/s1600/images.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-bI2Pj4YEzV0/TVXpjJTVM5I/AAAAAAAADZI/1Je6dlxs3To/s1600/images.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Be aware that he\u2019ll have a hard time making up his mind, and will, most likely, not want to let go of most of his things. But gently remind him of his goal to change and find order, happiness, and peace---to reclaim his home. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">All hoarders firmly believe that every single object will be useful one day, whether it is a broken toy, old magazine, torn ill fitting shoes, empty container, plastic bag , old tooth brushes, old school notebooks, old damaged &nbsp;music tapes .. They will have an imaginary emotional connection to all such garbage.</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow;\">Rings a familiar bell , right? &nbsp;Well be aware!</span><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-tUqIA14UWlM/TVXpqDhS_cI/AAAAAAAADZM/Pprjy5NDQEQ/s1600/images+%25281%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-tUqIA14UWlM/TVXpqDhS_cI/AAAAAAAADZM/Pprjy5NDQEQ/s1600/images+%25281%2529.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Hoarders are afraid to throw away things, this is why it is a mental disease. Hoarders live with so much clutter it may endanger their physical health. Dirt, mites, ticks , insects, and bacteria that form over a period of time can cause sickness and unhappiness. Excessive paper and cloth in a home can cause a fire.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-FlY_68eAoWg/TVXpvbOuTDI/AAAAAAAADZQ/Na8U3u_FbuI/s1600/images+%25284%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-FlY_68eAoWg/TVXpvbOuTDI/AAAAAAAADZQ/Na8U3u_FbuI/s1600/images+%25284%2529.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Compulsive hoarding can have an adverse effect on a family. Family members who share a home with the hoarder cannot understand why their loved one keeps so many useless garbage . It prevents the family from enjoying their home. Inmates get allergy, &nbsp;Rhinitis and get depressed for no rhyme or reason. Functional spaces are lost due to clutter.&nbsp; For example, table tops occupy useless stuff. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">The family of the hoarder is ashamed of bringing their friends home. There is no happiness or love.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Hoarders make themselves miserable and and everyone else miserable.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">People with personality disorders , generally, blame others for their problems</span>. They are awful to work with because they don\u2019t accept responsibility for themselves and therefore never change.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Remember, there is NO medicine for treating hoarding. This OCD is due to bad programming in your genes. You need to wipe out the blue print and insert a healthy one.&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: large;\">Vipassana meditaion </span>is one sure way. &nbsp;Read my post dated 9<sup>th</sup> Feb 2011, and change for the better.</span>&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">It is about letting go first and then changing for the better. You can never learn, unless you unlearn.</span><o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br /></span></span>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<object width=\"320\" height=\"266\" class=\"BLOGGER-youtube-video\" classid=\"clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000\" codebase=\"http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=6,0,40,0\" data-thumbnail-src=\"http://img.youtube.com/vi/sxZsOXsePHo/0.jpg\"><param name=\"movie\" value=\"http://youtube.googleapis.com/v/sxZsOXsePHo&source=uds\" /><param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#FFFFFF\" /><param name=\"allowFullScreen\" value=\"true\" /><embed width=\"320\" height=\"266\"  src=\"http://youtube.googleapis.com/v/sxZsOXsePHo&source=uds\" type=\"application/x-shockwave-flash\" allowfullscreen=\"true\"></embed></object></div>\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br /></span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-SaJ_uxJTpgg/TVXpVoyjPLI/AAAAAAAADY8/LsFnZCq9O5A/s1600/P4270001.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"320\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-SaJ_uxJTpgg/TVXpVoyjPLI/AAAAAAAADY8/LsFnZCq9O5A/s320/P4270001.JPG\" width=\"296\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p>&nbsp;CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL</o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><o:p>..</o:p></span></div>\n</div>\n", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "16", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/1963295117232337821/comments"}}, {"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "5349653338194067065", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2011-02-11T20:34:00+05:30", "updated": "2011-02-11T20:52:13+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxMjk3NDM3NzMzNTA3Cm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2011/02/naive-sailor-ship-manoevering-capt-ajit.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/5349653338194067065", "title": "THE NAIVE SAILOR, SHIP MANOEUVRING -- CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: left;\" trbidi=\"on\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-0C1jlXdAEEY/TVVOsa6ItgI/AAAAAAAADY4/NE9HJDEWqfA/s1600/chm.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-0C1jlXdAEEY/TVVOsa6ItgI/AAAAAAAADY4/NE9HJDEWqfA/s1600/chm.jpg\" /></a></div><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">I was coming out of a long river in USA, having loaded a full ship of Styrene Monomer.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The river pilot, gave me his calling card which is unusual. Obviously he was proud of who he was. It was punched on the card , that he was the Chief Examiner for Pilots in that neck of the woods.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">We started idle talk after a while , and then he tells me he has seen ice bergy bits floating in the river, very often and how mysterious the river is\u2014blah blah. . Obviously the terminal / barges have been pigging their chemical pipelines into the river. As soon a Styrene hits the dirty water, it polymerises, and then floats like ice sheets.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Noticing the lack of awareness, I told him . \u201c I know you are the honourable Chief Examiner, would you like to submit yourself to an examination orals. &nbsp;I have been in command for 28 years, and at the end of the orals exam session I guarantee, you will be much wiser, and will be glad that you showed some humility and kept your &nbsp;ego in cold storage\u201c<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">He agreed, which shows that he had professional maturity and was interested in learning from a experienced sea Master.&nbsp;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">A sea Master is NOT a one trick pony.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The gist of a 1 hour session is as follows. Of an orals session, where i corrected his answers, with detailed explanations and diagrams.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">On a ship with fixed right hand propeller, every pilot will ask \u201c Captain bow goes to starboard, when propeller goes astern \u201c<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">I would say \u201c Nope, The stern goes to port\u201d<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Which is true , as the pivoting centre is always towards the bows. When ship squats and is down by the head the pivoting centre is on the forecastle.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The pivoting centre shifts forward as the ship picks up speed. This is due to the water pressure on the bows.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">When you drop both the anchors at anchorage the pivoting centre is between both the hawse pipes. This information is very important to ships who drop their anchor , to prevent running aground. If only the stbd anchor is used, the pivot will be on the stbd hawse pipe.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Knowing the pivoting centre is crucial , to determine where you will tell the tug to push or pull. A tug pushing exactly on the pivot cannot achieve anything. The ship is a lever, which tips at the fulcrum or the pivot.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">This is why the bow thruster does a good job when the ship has speed less than 3 knots. When the ship moves faster , the pivot shifts forward. The feeble bow thruster has a smaller lever on the forward part of the fulcrum. &nbsp;Now if you have a stern thruster it will have a longer lever aft of the fulcrum and will turn the ship easily. It is NOT about the bow wave build up etc --Blah Blah.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Now why does the stern go to port when the RH propeller goes astern. All the books written by the white man talks about Transverse thrust, Screw race, Wheeling action\u2014blah blah.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If a propeller will wheel the ship stern to port, while going astern like a car wheel on terra firma, then what prevents it from doing the reverse , when the propeller goes ahead? &nbsp;Pray?<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Now, if you are on all fours, supporting your body with your two hands and legs, and I creep up from behind, and give you a resounding kick on your stbd side ass, which way will your stern go? Simple\u2014your ass will be thrown to port and your head will go to stbd. &nbsp;This is exactly what happens to the ship.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The RH propeller blades have a skew. When the propeller goes astern, the wash on the port quarter misses the hull and goes away . While the wash on the stbd hits the hull by the stern, or the stbd ass of the ship. This is why when you go astern you always go to the stbd bridge wing, to check out the propeller wash, to decide when exactly to let go anchor. The stbd wash gets channeled &nbsp;to the bridge front first.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">When the propeller moves ahead, there is no wash hitting the hull. This is why there is NO wheeling action, when the propeller moves ahead.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">When you manoeuvre it is important to know that the GPS speed is just the speed of the GPS antenna over the ground. It does NOT give ships speed.. For a long ship, with the pivot right forward, a swinging stern will show good speed on the GPS. It will show you the course of the GPS antenna of course.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">When you take a tight turn is is most important to start swinging well. For ships with aft accommodation, it acts like a huge sail. When you have a fresh wind from the port beam , it is easier to swing the ship to port.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">I remember coming out of the Parana river and just before dropping the senior most pilot of Buenos Aires / Recalada, he says \u201c I am passing astern of the pilot vessel, so that if the ships engines fail, the wind will blow the ship away from the pilot ship\u201d . I said \u201c This is exactly the reason why you should pass ahead of the pilot ship. To prove a point, I stopped the engines, and the pilot was surprised to see the ship heading exactly on a collision course, like magic . He did acknowledge how wrong he was, all these years.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">On large ships when two tugs pull you off the berth, you must know that as soon as the pilot gives a forward momentum, the pivot will shift forward, giving the aft tug a longer lever on the fulcrum, and hence more practical power. The tug at the bows , getting a shorter lever, will pull harder to make up and keep the ship\u2019s bows from swinging away. This is the time the tug lines part. Ship making fast tugs with modern hawsers doing figure of eight on bollard must be very careful. These modern ropes do NOT have friction coefficient. It is better to take two round turns on each bitt and then put a figure of eight. Surge means the rope will part with severe injury or loss of life. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Ships coming out of Houston river, after dropping pilot, gives full ahead, and then puts the helm on auto pilot. During which time, the helmsman, will take down the flags etc. &nbsp;You would have notices that the ship yaws from one side to another, basically the stern swinging wildly like a pendulum , with the fulcrum on the bulbous bows, due to less water under keel and squat. Less water under the ship means that the rudder does not bite, due to the vacuum effect. This is the time that the wheel must be taken on hand, and hand steering done till the water is deeper.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">While in rivers, make sure that your ship does NOT get jack-knifed by the forces of wind and current, catching ford and aft sections, selectively. The aft accommodation acts like a sail for the wind , and the deep bows catches the current under the water.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ZB6iuiVfQCE/TVVOXya5N5I/AAAAAAAADY0/Wih20-DiBZg/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ZB6iuiVfQCE/TVVOXya5N5I/AAAAAAAADY0/Wih20-DiBZg/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">..</span></div></div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. blue;\">Brits use minus screw driver, while the Yanks use plus&nbsp;</span></i><br />\n<i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></i><br />\n<i><span Anyone who disregards these provisions and takes any kind of action which conflicts with them will immediately be regarded as having disputed the will, and shall suffer the consequences of so doing.\"<o:p></o:p></span></span></i></div>\n<div style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot;
